ElI. INTRODUCTION
i1. CONTENTS AND STUDY AREA
The study area included the Paraguay, Paana. and Uruguay rivers' floodplains. This is a macrosystem
I         containing diverse subsystems differing in their structure and function. Its ecological stability depends on the
conservation of such heterogeneity. Men activities lead to environrental simplification, and a deterioriation of its
abiotic and biotic components. In most of the area man has extended its range to the floodplain. We suggest thatwithtin
the anthropic envirornent the potential negative impacts from the structures for protection against fluds should be less
significant than those caused by floods when these structures are lacking. We evaluated the adequacy of these -ttructures
I         considering those currently existent and those programmed for the near future, a special point to be dealt with in order to
recommend future trends of urban expansion.
I
2. ENVIRONMENTAL ANALYSIS
The main environmental components for the Flood Control Project are summarized as shown in Fig. I.2. (see
main report. page 4).
3. OBJECTIVES
The main objectives are directed to describe the most relevant environmental features of the Paraguay. Parana,
and Uruguay rivers flood plains, regarding their abiotic, biotic and anthropic components, and their conformity with the
pulsatile regime. The obtained basic information has been used to assess those potential environmental impacts that
I         would be produced by the flood control projects.:
I         4. SOURCES OF IFORMATION
Different Governmental Entities were relevated. Edited infornations required revisions of Scientific Libraries,
I         i.e., the School of Natural Sciences. National University of La Plata, the National Institute of Limnology (INALI), the
Northeastern Center of Applied Ecology (CECOAL). The INALI also facilitated us satellite images from the studied
area. The Institute of Technology (ZITEC) from Santa Fe was particularly helpful to solve methodological problems,
specially concerning cartography.
5. ZONIFICATION
0Zonification was based on images. maps, and tables including the most relevant aspects concerning floods.
Composite MSS color scanning images MSS (4,5 and 7 bands) were processed from the Parani river at the highest
recent flood (1983). MSS digital products (Landsat 5) from the same areas during a dry period (July, 1987) were also
utlitized. Images were adapted to the IDRISI formnat (480 x 500; Easunan, 1990). Scanned images were converted from
PCX to JPEG formnt by means of the Aldus Photolister Program. Thus, color became redder as contrast and saturation
increased. This made it possible to contrast the vegetation which emerged above the river water during flood. To
recognise water covered areas only band 7 was used. A special pallette was designed to constrast water (rose) and
vegetation (green). Furthernore, the normalized for vegetation difference (ND7) and the chromaticity indexes were
processed, the latter contrasting suspended material.
IH. THE PHYSICAL ENVIRONMENT

I.
1. INTRODUCTION
3                Regional climate, geology, geoniorphology, and hydrology are described and related to floods.
I    2 REGIONAL CLIMATE AND HYDROLOGY.
2. I.Climate
I                The  Koppen System of Climate Classification was adopted. Based upon the simultaneous analysis of
temperature and rainfall, together with the distribution of vegetation units, climate groups and subgroups could be
E         defined. Different regions in the studied area were defined as follows:
Aw: tropicaL mean annual temperature higher than I 8C, annual rainfall abundant, except in winter (dry season).
Cwa: temperate and wrnm, mean temperure higher than 22C in summner and dry winter.
Cra: temperate and warnm without dry season.
I         BSh: serniarid. annual rainfall not exceding 750 mrn and annual mean temperpture higher than 1°C.
H. temperature exhibits narked daily changes, rainfall are scarce.
E         2.2. Hydrologv
Paran Rtim
It drains 1,600,000 kmr. Sixty percent of its area is located in Brazil. Three sections can be distinguished:
a) High Parand : from the confluence of Paranarba and Grande rivers in Brazil up to its confluence with Paraguay river.
After Iguazit river enters its left margin the Parani river limits Argentina and Paraguay as Iguazu river is a border
between Argentina and Brazil. It runs through a stepping plateau with numerous water falls, the most important being
Cataratas del Iguazii. Intense forest cutting has desvastated large areas of the native woods, only the four percent of it is
leit. Therefbre, the soil has been eroded increasing the sedimentarv load downstream.
I         b) Middle Panansi: from the confluence with the Paraguay up to Rosario. The most relevant characteristic of this
section is the increase of the floodplain width. The bluffs on the left margin are particularly remarkable: they are exposed
to severe erosion.
c) Lower Parana . from Rosario up to its confluence with the Uruguay river, where it opens into "Delta del Parani",
which has a length of 300 km and a surface of 15.000 kmn.
Paraeuanv River
Its basin exhibits an extense alluvial plain with very low topographic gradient. Its watershed covers 1,I00,000
I         krnm, from sierras So Parecis and Tombador, Brazil. up to its confluence with the Parane, being its main trait the Xarayes
Pantanal. a wetland of 100,000 krn'. through which the Euvial system drains; it influences decisively on the drainage and
floods of this section. Its trbutaries, Pilcornayo and mainly Bermejo supply a high sedimentary load. The Pilcomayo and
the Paraguay are the border between Argentina and Paraguay up to its confluence with the ParaniL
I         Urunuav River
Its drainagc basin covers 440,000 km2 in Brazil. Argentina. and Uruguay. It is the border between Argentina
I         and the other two countries. Ln its lower section. together with the Parani joins the Rio de la Plata. The volurme of water
is relativeky low and hvdrograms are less complex Anyway, there are man-made reservoirs in Brasil, and specially
i         remarkable in Salto Grande between Concordia (Argentina) and Salto (Uruguay). Aguapey, MlriBSay, MocoretA and
Gualeguaychu rivers are its most important afluents.
Rainfal
3



Mean annuaL monthly fluctuations and variations among different years records are illustrated in Fig. m.I.
E        Wtthin the study area, It is remarkable the lowering gradient from the cast (2,400-1,400 nan) to the west (400 nun). The
highest mean annual rainfal records were obtained along the Iguaza and the high Uruguay.
I         Fiefds
Due to the heavy rains in the upper sections, its elongated shape and its narrow flood plain, the Uruguay basin
I        exhibits the highest discharge vauiability, both intra-annual and annual. The highest maxmum annual discharge was
recorded in the region in 1983. Droughts are much more severe in the Uruguay than in Parani/Paraguay system.The
mean discharge of the Parana river is 12,000 el/s in the rniddle section, with minimum and maxmum historical values of
I        4,000 m'/s and 60,000 m`/s respectively.
Water Levels
Regarding different years and monthly averaged records, water level variations in Parana (Entre Rios) have 7.9
E         m amplitude (January, 1904 - February, 1995). The highest rise of water level commonly takes place in fall (March-
April), as a result of the rains occurring in the high basin section. Lowering of water levels occurs by the end of winter
and beginning of spring (August-October). At irregular intervals, extaordinary water rises, resulting in floods of higher
temporal extent.
3. GEOLOGICAL FRAMEWORK
U                Two basins characterise the studty area: the Chaco Paranense Basin, comprising sedimentary units ranging in
age from the Palaeozoic to the Cenozoic, is the most extended within the region; the other basin, specific to the study
area, is the Parni Basin, mainly composed of outcroping basaltic rocks with intercalations of sandstones. The latter
I         unit is almost restricted to the province of Misiones.
E    4. GEOMORPROLOGY AND HYDROLOGY
The most extended units lie on the Chaco Paranense Basin, where river flood plains, the Chaco Paranense
Plain, the Iberi Depression, the Parana Delta and the Entre Rios "Cuchillas" are typical landforms. The Misiones
Plateau is the other geomorphic unit mostly developed in the province of Misiones. The lower Paraguay exhibits a
sinuous to meandering pattern with disactivated meanders at both channel margins. On the right margin, one of the most
I         important tributaries, the Bermqo, shows a typical meandering pattern . The mniddle Parani river is strongly
anastomosed with numerous islands, several imbricated. The higher Parani has an average yield of 12,000 n9Is and a
suspended load of 100 x 10 tlyear. This section flows through a basaltic plateau down to Posadas, and becomes an
E         alluvial river dowstream from this city, until it reaches the confluence with the Paraguay river. Middle Parana flows for
more than 1,100 km through an alluvial plain between 6-40 km wide. Its mean yield is 16,000 m'Ys. This section also
receives the sedirnentary contribution from the Paraguay river. The sedimentary load at Corrientes is 392 x I0' t/year.
On the left margin, the river forms bluffs; the floodplain extends on the right margin up to Diamante where the upper
"Delta Entrerriano" develops. The lower Parani extends from 300 km from Rosario to its confluence with the Uruguay
I         river, forming the 15,000 km: "Parani Delta'. Although the Uruguay river watershed is much smaEler than the Pararia
basin, It drains more than 250,000 km- through 1,700 kmn with an average yield of 4,600 m'fs. In its upper course it
runs through a bending canyon (Province of Misiones) down to te Corientes-Misiones border. Here the river leaves
I         the canyon and reaches the tail of Salto Grande Dam Lake. A 150 km long alluvial plain extends southward from Salto
Grande. Between Col6n and Gualeguaychui the river changes abruptly its course from N-S to E-W for about 30 kmh and
then it resumes southwards, suggesting a structural control. The main sediments of the Uruguay river are sands and
gravels.
m. FLOOD ANALYSIS
I                                                            4
I.



1. PHYSICAL ASPECTS
During the hydric event 1982/83, the waters covered almost the whole alluvial plain . The "Delta
Entrerriano' was flooded in a section of about 50 km wide. According to documented data this episode can be
U        catalogued as secular.
2. HISTORIC ANALYSIS
As it was recently suggested by Sir W  Halerow & Partners:
3         * From 1965, the more important recorded flood events were related to the Paranh, in Posadas andCorrientes.
+ In Paraguay river most of the events cfhigh magnitude recorded from 1810 occurred from 1965
* From ten events in the Uruguay, recorded from 1898, four occurred after 1972.
The above referred records mean that flood incidence in 'Cuenca del Plata " in the last three or four decades.
Regarding the four more significant events during the XX Century, the one occurring in 1982/19B3 was the
most severe. Its occurrence can be attributed to the heavy rainfall that was recorded between June 1982 and May 1983.
the highest in the present Century.The most important observed impacts in the hydrometeorology of the basin were most
probably influenced by human intervention, as follows:
I       *  changes of lana use, specially forest cutting and. consequently increase of discharge levels.
* Hydroelectric enterprises mainly in the Alto Parand. in BraziL with regulating effect resulting in lower yields.
* Rainfall increase during the wet season at least from 1960, suggestive of climate changes induced by man.
3. DAMAGE EVALUATION
Flooding events that took place in 1983 exhibited significantly higher impact than those occurring in 1992; this
I         evaluation is based on:
* the number of evacuated people
* the number of houses impacted
+ the econonic costs
* the flooded areas
l
V. THIE BIOTIC EiNIRONMENT
1. THIE PULSATILE REGIME OF THE GREAT RIVERS AND THEIR INFLUENCE ON
|    THE BIOTA
In the studied basin we observed that the turnover rate of biotic and abiotic components in the islands is higher
than in the periphery. Thus, organism longevity is higher in the flood valley margins. Change rates are directly related to
I         the time elapsed while these landscapes are connected to the rivers. Human interventions can alter the organization
patterns of landscapes, and the energy and material fluxes which normally maintain the ecosystems biodiversity and
productivity.
H  2. WETLANDS
I                                                            S
l



Some of the most representative wetlands from the flood valley were described being their locadons punctually
I          mapped although without including their geographic range; they are: Rio Pilcomayo and Laguna Blanca, Wetlands fiomn
Parque Nacional Chaco, Isla del Cerrito, Bajos Submeridionales, Esteros del IberiLower Parani Swamps
3. VEGETATION
The most important vegetation observed units were: Gallery Forest, Natural High Forest, and Aquatic
Macrophytes. Succession, main communities, zonification, and flood impact on vegetation were described in the P&rana
Valley. The gallery forest was severely damaged during the hydric events of 1982-83 and 1992. The mechanical effects
were significant at the lower topographic gradients, resating in plant destruction and ultimately in floating accumulation
of rooted out plants.
4. FISH
The Parani river houses more than 220 fish species, twenty of them of economic value. Due to its role in
the throphic web, and its commercial importance, the "aibalo"(Prochilodus lineatus) is the key species in the system.
NMigrations in the Parana river flodplain are stimulated by reproduction. throphic demands, and by seasonal and
hydrological changes.
S. VERTEBRATES (EXCLUDING FISHES)
|                Floodings are responsible of passive geographic species dispersion, local mnigrations of aquatic birds due to
changes ir, throphic available items and reduction/extinction of foraging habitats, and increase of mortality rat- of
terrestrial species which invade the inundated flood valley during periods previously dry.
6. DEPTERA VECTORS OF DISEASES
The study area is represented by several dipteran vectors. We documented the geographic range in the study
area of dipterans potential vectors of oncnocercosis, leishmaniasis, yellow feber, dengue ,and malaria. Limnotopes
generated in the inner margins of defenses can favor the setting of water born diseases vectors.
I    V.FLOODINGS: A1N ECOLOGICAL APPROACH
Ii1. INTRODUCTION
The ecology of floodings and droughts was analyzed regarding the adaptive responses of the different
organismic units .
I        2. R1VERS AS MACROSYSTEMS'
Different traits exhibited by the studied South Anerican rivers were analyzed taking into account the dominant
processes occurring during floods and droughts, considering the basic natural components, and  the anthropic
environment, as integrated in a complex of ecosystems.

E IV. THE ANTHROPIC ENVIRONMNT
1. REGIONAL CONTEXT
Within the regional range the fitness displayed by the different social strata were described taking into account
the historic and cultural factors influencing their way of lie.
2. CULTURAL INHERITANCE
The main considered archaeological regions were "Misionera", 'Paranct Centrar, 'Dltica', and  Urzguay
Central' Three main periods were recogrnized: Pre-ceramic, Early Potter, and Laze Potter. The Hispanic-Indigenous
period also included first contacts between indians and Spanish colonizers.The influence of Franciscan and Jesuits during
about 200 years (1575- 1767) on the indigenous settlements weres desct ibed and mapped.
I           3. COLONIZATION AND MIGRATORY FLUXES.
After the Jesuits expulsion (1767) the indigenous groups were dominant until the end of the X1X Century when
inmigrants from Europe played a decisive role in the population growth, distribution, and in the mral and industrial
I           development.
U           4. REGIONAL SOCIAL AND ECONONMC CONTEXTS.
According to their differential fitness to the natural periodically flood ecosytems, three main strata were
distinguished in the study area: islander settlements, periurban settlements, and cities or towns located within the
floodplain. Home confort is highly limited in the alluvial valley, specially in the provinces of Fornosa, Misiones and
Chaco, with about 60 % of deficitary houses. The population numbers were not necessarily related to the provincial
surface; this is particularly valid if Misiones is considered; although this province surface is much lesser than that of the
the acronym FITRAS condense the following words: frequency. intensity. tension. recurrency, amplitude. and seasonality
7



remaining ones, its population number is sirnilar to those of Corrientes and Chaco. Despite some improvement recorded
U        during the last decade, education is highly deficitary at all levels in all the regarded provinces. The situation is still
deficitary at the pfimary level with dramatic dilutions of the student population from the first to the second degree.
Among the northeastern provinces Santa Fe has the highest participation with 9.8 % of the National Gross Product. The
remaining provinces have a much lower participation from little more than 3 % (Entre Rios) to less than I %
I        (Forrnosa).The diversity of Agricultural activities was compared between the included provinces. In  a  global sense,
infrastructure referred to transportation in the alluvial valley is still in a deficitary situation, mainly in the Oriental Chaco.
I         Enfant mortality trend is declining in the studied area, but still higher than 20/1.000, and reaching almost 33 /1,000 in
Chaco and Formosa. The number of beds/ 1,000 inhabitants in hospitals ranges between 2 and 3. The number of
physicians /10,000 inhabitants ranges between 19 and 40. The main causes of mortality are similar in the different
provinces (cardiopathics. tumors, traumatisms, parasites, poisoning, etc.).
VUL.REGIONAL  ENVIRONMENTAL  PROBLEMS  AND  FLOODS.
IDENTIFICATION AM) PROPOSALS.
II1. URBAN AND PERIUPBAN ECOSYSTEMS
The urban and periurban ecosystems are not well adapted to the floods caused either by hydrometric rises or by
hmeavy rains. The main environmental problems are due to inadequate human settling in area periodically flooded which
I       are more susceptible to sanitary risks. Frequently the pumping systems are deficitary and drainage is limited. Other
environmental oroblcm can arise when defense material are xtracted from inadequate loan areas where the generated
depression can be occupied by water sooner or later contamninated and/or invaded by aquatic plants and eventually by
disease vectors.
Mitigation to these problems could be attained by:
I .       * adequate urban expansion planning.
- adequate sypply of pumping systems.
* adequate selection of loan areas.
Terrapleins persistence depends on diverse enviromnental factors. Hydric erosion is most probably the key
factor and its impacts magnitude is directly related to the terraplein vulnerability, which is conditioned by the
properties of the material selected for its building (granulometry, cohesivity, compactness,etc.). Fixation vegetal
structures are profitable. specially if their expansion and aereal and subterranean development are carefuilly adapted to
every particular situation. Other problems wothly to remark are the waste and water accumulation on the side slopes.
I
2. NATURAL ECOSYSTEMS
The most expresive changes operate as wooded areas are overexploited. These impacts indirectly affect soil
protection, faunal species stability, and hydric resource regulation. The forest is composed by some species which are
seriously threatened by human intervention, remarkably: Tabebuia ipe ("lapacho negro"), Schinopsis balansae
("quebracho colorado"), Aspidosperma ("palo rosa"), Euterpe edulis ("palmito') and Astronium balansae ("urunday").
Several rnamrnal and bird species housed by tnese wooded areas are at high risk.The 1982183 hydric events caused
irreversible damages in about 50 % of the trves from the gallery forest of the lower Paraguay river.
I                  lThe most remarkable problems of the Natural Protected Areas from the study area can be summarized as follows:
* Only 5.6 % is protected, if the Ibei Depression were excluded the figure would fall to 1.6%.
||         * More than 50 % ofthe known protected areas cover less than 10 kn:.
* Most of the provincial and municipal protected areas are deficitaiy in several aspects inaucture for administration,
1             police efficiency, qualified staff econornic support).

4. INSTrTCIONAL ORGANIZATION
The treatment of environmental problems in the region is limited by the lack of unified criteia among the diffrent

5.THE ENV[RONMENT AND ITS lMPACT ON TERRAPLEINS
Most probably ,the main natural environmental impact on terrapleins is due to hydric erosion which magritude
depends on the material they are built with, their lack of maintenance and the occurrence of unexpected rains and
Sfloods.

RESJMIEN
Este Informe incluye informacion acerca de los rasgos ambientales del medioffsico, bidticoy eco-social de la
llanura de inundacion vinculado a los grandes rios sudamericanos que incursionan en territorio argentino: los
rios Paraguway Parani y Uruguay. El traramiento de los diferentes topicos abordados ha sido tomado como
base para el anailisis de la incidencia de los pulsos de inundacidn tanto en los procesos namrwales como on los
dmbitos urbano. periurbano y ruraL Se analizanpreliminarmente los evenwales impactos direcros o indirectos
I               de las inundaciones y de las obras de defensa sobre los componentes del medio, asi como aquellos del ambienre
sobre las obras de defensa Los resultados obtenidos han seruido de base para la identificacion de los
principales problemas ambientales, laformulaci6n de propuestas tendientes a su mitigacion y la estimaci6n de
los beneficios esperados a partir de tales propuestas. Asimismo. se proponen cursos de accion para elfuturo,
con especial enfasis en la necesidad de realLzar esrudios adicionales ms prolongados.

2.2. Hidrologia
E         2.2.1. Caudales
La cuenca del Uruguay tiene un escurrimiento mayor, debido fiudamentalmente a lluvias mis fuertes en
su cuenca superior. En 1983 se produjo en toda la region el caudal mAximo anual registrado en un afo
calcndario, con cl doble del caudal mdlio anual en todas las cuencas. El r6gimen do sequin del Uruguay es
mucho mis severo que en el sistems sistema ParanA/Paraguay. El almaconarniento natural de la cuenca del
Uruguay es muucho menor. por lo que el pase de caudales do un afDo a otro es muy pequeflo. La maxima sequia
ocurri6 en 1917, cuando se registr6 solo el 15% del caudal media anual en Concordia. En el sistema del
Parani/Paraguay 1934 fue cl aflo mis pobre del registro dispanible (63% del caudal medio anual en Corrientes).
La distribucion estacional de los caudales anuales rauestra la complejidad hidrol6gica de la cuenca. La
I         Fig. 11.5 exhibe el caudal medio mensual como cl porcentaje del caudal medio anual en cuatro puntos, do donde
surge:
I         a) En Posadas la distribucion estacional del caudal as la esperada en base al patrin estacional de precipitaciones,
teniendo en cuenta los efectos do retardo en una cuenca tan gande; los caudales promedio mis altos ocurren
entrc diciembre y abril.
K         b) En Puerto Bermejo, sobre el Paraguay, el esquema se revierte completamente. Los flujos de entrada al
Pantanal siguen la distribuci6n estarional esperada. per el almaenamiento natural es tan grande que cl flujo de
salida se demora hasta scis mesas. Aguas abajo del Pantanal, los caudales promedio mis altos ocurren entre
agosto y noviembre.
c) En Corrientes, la integraci6n de estos dos regimcnes de caudal tiene como consecuencia una distribuci6n mis
I         pareja del caudal promnedio a lo largo del afDo. Podria suponerse que la compensacion de las estaciones de
caudales pico en cl Parani y cl Paraguay reduce la intesidad del riesgo de inundaci6n aguas abajo de la
confluencia. Sin embargo, esto no es enteramente asi, ya que la distribucion estacional del riesgo de inundaci6n
es zius compleja que lo que sugiere la marcha anual de los caudales medios mensuales.
d) En Concordia, dicha marcha no parece reflejar, a primers vista, la distuibuci6n estacional de precipitaciones
que indica la OEA (1969) pam la cuonca superior, que es relativamente uniforme mes s mes mnientras que los
caudales se presentan con Un penodo intenso de caudales bajos entre enero v mano. Esta discrepancia pareceria
sugerir quc en dichos meses el escurrimiento es bajo.

De acuerdo con las caractistias del paisaje resultante, de muy escasa pendiente, comicnza a

I              climfiticos acaccidos a partir de los utimos dos rnillones de afhos. Los colectores principales de dicha red
comienzan a desarrollar asi planicies aluviales, cuyas magnitudes sorha detenninadas por la litologia de las Areas

Dado este hecho y la muy esca pendiente, hay tamnbicn procesos do acumulaci6n con la consecuente

Ya a la altura de la localidad de Dimante y siempre en cuanto a la relaci6n > carp s6lida vs. c

Las caracterfsticas indicadas par este gran sisterna fluvial corresponden preponderanrtemnte a los
patrones tipicos de los denorninados "rios aluviales" (Schummn, 1985), cuyos caracteres comunes son la

Etre las prncipales caracwtisticas de estos eventos hidricos. que afectan al ecosistena y al hombre,

m. ANALISIS DE LAS INUNDACIONES
1. ASPECTOS FISICOS
El total de imas inundadas incluyendo a las provincias afectadas (excepto Buenos Aires), fue superior

(Euterpe edulls) y el urunday (Astrotium balatsae)

3.EDUCACION
Adernas de la situaci6n deficitaria de los diferentes niveles de educaci6n en el ara de estudio, uno de los
principales problemas en este contexto concimne a la falta de una adecuada orientacion hacia los problemnas
vinculados a las inundaciones y otros colaterals. no menos importantes, a saber. disposicion de residuos
domiciliarios, disposicion de excretas, que en general se relacionancon una fa!ta de concientizai6n de los
pobladores en relaci6n con la problenatica inabiental.
Las limnitaciones expuestas detenan que, si bien las medidas estructurales tson de indudable beeficio
para la calidad de vida de los habitamnes del valle de inundaci6n, se imnpone la neccsaria implenentaci6n de medidas
no estmcturales, entre las cuales la educacion surge como prioritaria.
°El fortalecimiento de este aspecto es una de las acciones que deberi priorizame para optimizar las
medidas de mitigacion y contribuir asimismo a una mejor comprensi6n de la necesidad de modificar hibitos de
vida y tendencias de disibtrcio6n urbana Sin duda, que el destino de mayores esfumrszos y presupuestos hacia la
educaci6n tendri efectos tangibles en los cambios positivos que se espera logar en el medio social.
Lo expuesto da sustento a la propuesta de estudios adicionales tendientes a fortalecer el sistema

5. EL IMPACTO DEL AMBIIENTE SOBRE LAS OBRAS DE DEFENSA
Entre las numerosas causas que pueden afectar a las obras de defcnsa, las mis facilmente
detectables se pueden observar en les terraplenes (Figs. Vl.3, VIII.4, VIII.5, VT.6). Las nnis
*                importantes son: falta de mantenimiento, erosi6n hidrica, especialmente pluvial, intercalaci6n de materiales
de difercnte textura en las horizontes del pertil, uso indebido de terraplenes, fatta de mantenimicnto,
inundaciones de mayor magnitud y duraci6n que las esperadas, etc.
La precaria estabilidad de los terraptenes durante los primeros afios, a partir de su construcci6n.
puede exacerbarse por acci6n de diferentes agentes amnbientales; las mas aparentes son las lluvias
torrenciales y prolongadas y la actividad de animales cavadores. Entre los factores que actuan de un modo
I                 nmas criptico. aunque con real impacto negativo se destaca el en=alezamiento desordenado provocado por
cl desarrollo desordenado de plantas ruderales, cuyos principales efectos son: agravamiento de deficiencias
esteticas, inhibici6n de visualizaci6n de gietas o carcavas y generacicon de sitios propensos a la
acumulaci6n de residuos urbanos.                I
En terraplenes construidos con materiales friables. por refiulado y carentes de una cubierta
vegetal en los taludes y coronamientos, se puede producir considerable erosi6n y, eventualmente, su
destrucci6n parcial o total, perdiendose el efecto deseado de estas obras.
Neiffet al (1987) mencionan las ventajas que ofirecen los vegetales para la fijaci6n de taludes. En
I                este caso cobran importancia, su expansi6n. su desarrollo vertical aereo y subterraneo (estratificaci6n,
densidad, volumen y bifurcaci6n madicular). El componente aereo es importante en la atenuacicn de los
efectos negativos de la erosi6n hidrica y en el mantenimiento de tenores favorables de hurnedad en el
suelo. El componente subternineo brinda estabilidad estructural al suelo, favorece la circulaci6n vertical
del agua y la capacidad de su retenci6n, a la vez que por evapotranspiracion hacia la atm6sfera disminuye
los excedentes hidricos.

TABLA LX.7-. JERARQUIZACI6N AMBIENTAL DE IMPACTOS  tW 4.4S
|rZ6AS  arZ  =A1Lo /Ct             /4            4#4   OBO4S.
Color            Calificacl6        -   grado de
_____ _____   ____ _____ ____      impacto
3R                 critico
I;w; -2wj                  2N               importante
IA               moderado
E |              0ov                minimo
La calificaci6n se estableceen cada proyecto para dos escenatios, con y sin niedidas. y la
jerarquizacion global contempla las medidas de mitigaci6n.
Cada ficha esta complementada con un croquis (tomado de los planos del proyecto) que
esquematiza los elementos asociados a la problemitica de las crecidas del fio (o rios) y a las
Il                    soluciones propuestas. Ademas se incluyen en las fichas fotogrificas referentes a los
problernas ambientalcs actuales o susceptibles de desencadenarse o acentuarse con la
operacion de las obras.
En esta entrega se incluyen las fichas de evaluacion ambiental de Proycetos representativos,
en cuanto a la cobertura de los distintos tipos de problernas ambientales y soluciones
propuestas:
terraplenes en recinto, Goya (23)
J                                     terraplenes abiertos, Gualeguay (36)
rectificaciones y canalizaciones rurales. cuenca arroyo San Antonio (7)
rectificaciones y canalizaciones urbanas, Curuzu Cuatia (26)
3                                     drenajes pluviales Gualeguaychu (37)
puentes y accesos, subsistema Leyes-Setubal (14)
pozos, zanjas y canales drenantes, Diamante (33)
defensas costeras, alteos perimetrales, desag.es pluviales. Carnpana (42)
control de erosion fluvial mediante obras de hormig6n. Ayo. Saladillo (12)
4. CONCLUSIONES
a) Las obros del PPCI no produclrdn impactos ambienWaes a  nivel
regionai, ya que su presidn sobre .i ambente es pan  al en :e espaco
geogrdfico,  tayormente lUmhado a dreas uranasyperlurbanas donde los
amblentesyea e    persarbadp.
b) -la  implementacdtn  del programa  con  relacldn  a  los proyectos
especficos anajidos, lnclayendo las medias de nldgacldn propuesfos
generard consecuenclas ambientalesposltvas en las dreas de influencia de
las obras a realiz.         .
